  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_894977a3-9607-41ec-84bc-18e90a846247'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText5862285522451965444" style="display:none">When he becomes Lady Lyssa’s full servant, Jacob crosses the threshold into a darker relationship with her than he’s known before. His time as a vampire hunter certainly hadn’t prepared him to embrace a world where humans are sexual commodities, but he adapted. Now he finds the integrity of his soul challenged as he serves his Mistress’s needs as fully as he services her desires.<br /><br />The vampire world believes human servants are inferior, a vital source for their varying appetites. Jacob knows a human servant is far more than that. His Mistress needs a warrior, a friend and a lover. A man who will serve her in all ways, even if he has to betray the priceless treasure of her love.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_116805608" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116805608" />
    <a title="Ridley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley"><img alt="Ridley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251681007p2/2543252.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116805608?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ridley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ridley" href="/user/show/2543252-ridley">Ridley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2543252-ridley?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116805608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12811706971814966079">The second half of Vampire Queen Lady Lyssa and her human servant Jacob's story, started in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1285704.The_Vampire_Queen_s_Servant__Vampire_Queen___1_' title='The Vampire Queen's Servant (Vampire Queen, #1) by Joey W. Hill' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Queen's Servant</a>, this book was an entirely underwhelming experience. Despite a full plate of conflict - Lyssa's fatal disease, volatile vampire politics, the nature of the romantic relationship itself - I failed to connect with it emotionally and ended up skimming through sex scene and exposition alike.<br/><br/>To begin with, it's plagued with telling in the character-focused first half. Too often the </span>
  <span id="freeText12811706971814966079" style="display:none">The second half of Vampire Queen Lady Lyssa and her human servant Jacob's story, started in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1285704.The_Vampire_Queen_s_Servant__Vampire_Queen___1_" title="The Vampire Queen's Servant (Vampire Queen, #1) by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Queen's Servant</a>, this book was an entirely underwhelming experience. Despite a full plate of conflict - Lyssa's fatal disease, volatile vampire politics, the nature of the romantic relationship itself - I failed to connect with it emotionally and ended up skimming through sex scene and exposition alike.<br /><br />To begin with, it's plagued with telling in the character-focused first half. Too often the character would go and do something - like have a m/f/m threesome with Jacob, Lyssa and Jacob's brother Gideon - and then the author would go and expressly say why they did it in the POV prose - to relieve Gideon of his pressing loneliness and resentment, in the example I give. Not only is that my job as a reader to draw those conclusions on my own, I kept reading the explanations and disagreeing. Being managed by the author just kept me from connecting with the characters, and as there's little plot or action going on at this point, I was bored stiff.<br /><br />The plot does pick up about halfway through when the Vampire Scout Jamboree...uh, Council Meetings convene in South America. There's all manner of intrigue, politics and entertainment as hundreds of vampires and their servants convene for a vamp G7 summit. Unfortunately, between the charged bits of intrigue, there's a lot of gratuitous kinky sexual nonsense that left me cold. It felt like filler to me, but if you like unemotional group sex with penetrative statues or choreographed group anal sex that sounded like a cross between Broadway and a porno-style gangbang, then holy hell, is this the book for you. As a bonus offer if you order now, you also get penetrative sex with a winged gargoyle-like creature. Hurry, sale ends soon. <br /><br />The solution to Lyssa's disease opens up a whole host of other issues and spends no time at all dealing with them. The book ends as a steaming pile of deus ex machina lacking any emotional punch at all.<br /><br />To say I was disappointed is an understatement. I loved the emotion in the EC published book of hers that I read, so I'm really surprised to have found these books to be emotional flatliners. I've heard great things about book four in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6149219.Beloved_Vampire__Vampire_Queen___4_" title="Beloved Vampire (Vampire Queen, #4) by Joey W. Hill" rel="nofollow noopener">Beloved Vampire</a>, so I may still read that. Maybe these two were a fluke. I don't know.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12811706971814966079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_228607176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228607176" />
    <a title="Tevya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2629035-tevya"><img alt="Tevya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463192555p2/2629035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228607176?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tevya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tevya" href="/user/show/2629035-tevya">Tevya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228607176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15091886684804669342">Reviewed on Reading Lark: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://readinglark.blogspot.com/2011/11/book-review-mark-of-vampire-queen.html'>http://readinglark.blogspot.com/2011/...</a><br/><br/>This is the second of the Vampire Queen series. In the first book, The Vampire Queen's Servant, we find Jacob struggling to gain the acceptance of Lady Lyssa, to earn his third mark to become her full servant and prove to her that he has what it takes to be a human servant. Through a battle of the wills, he accomplishes his goal and they settle into a not so easy routine of preparing for the Council Meeting. The Mark of the Vampir</span>
  <span id="freeText15091886684804669342" style="display:none">Reviewed on Reading Lark: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://readinglark.blogspot.com/2011/11/book-review-mark-of-vampire-queen.html">http://readinglark.blogspot.com/2011/...</a><br /><br />This is the second of the Vampire Queen series. In the first book, The Vampire Queen's Servant, we find Jacob struggling to gain the acceptance of Lady Lyssa, to earn his third mark to become her full servant and prove to her that he has what it takes to be a human servant. Through a battle of the wills, he accomplishes his goal and they settle into a not so easy routine of preparing for the Council Meeting. The Mark of the Vampire Queen opens with a dramatic prologue, fueling the belief that Jacob and Lyssa are soul mates who have been together for centuries, through two of Jacob's previous lives. This emotional and sentimental prologue sets the tone for this second book. We have moved past the violent battle of the wills between two alphas and moved to place where lovers are struggling to protect what is theirs while enjoying the last of their time together. It is not an easy ride, as the two are far from equals, but there is a definite shift in the undercurrent of the story.<br /><br />First of all, I have to say this: Best. Prologue. Ever! If I hadn't already been drawn into the story from the first book, that prologue alone would have sucked me in. It made my heart break for Lady Lyssa's loss of her Knight, while also showing me that Jacob had in fact, come to Lyssa's aid more than this once over her centuries of life. Her previous servant Thomas, the scholarly monk, held the belief that Jacob and Lyssa were soul mates and that Jacob had been in Lyssa's life twice before their current partnering. According to Thomas, Jacob comes to Lyssa when she needs him most, when her life is in danger, and her life is most certainly in danger right now. Not only is Lady Lyssa facing a terminal illness, but she is also facing the fact that she has doomed the one person on earth she has ever loved to death along with her. Together she and Jacob must find a way to save the refugees in her territory while keeping her illness a secret.<br /><br />As much as I loved The Vampire Queen's Servant, I loved this one even more. The emotions were so much stronger, and I loved watching Lyssa come to terms with the fact that Jacob was more than just her servant. The two became such a unit, a true couple in many ways, through the course of this book. Lyssa finally allowed herself to be vulnerable and to trust Jacob with her heart, and she finally admitted to herself and to Jacob that she did in fact love him. Both Jacob's and Lyssa's reactions to these new-found feelings were so much fun to anticipate, and I have to admit that both characters surprised me on more than one occasion.<br /><br />There was enough action and suspense to keep me guessing. I absolutely adored the scene at the faire for Jacob's birthday; total swoon moments aplenty! Through the whole book, I kept steeling myself for Lyssa's (and thus Jacob's) death. Surely they wouldn't really die, right? I mean - how could they?! All I will say about that scene is that I have never cried that hard during a book in my life. I'm talking blubbering all over my pillow, barely able to see the words to keep reading crying. <br /><br />And while the ending was absolutely perfect, it left me wanting more. Other than the complete shift in tone and emotion in this book, another significant difference for me was that I met other vampire master/servant and mistress/servant couples who I wanted to know more about. In the first book, all I cared about were Lyssa and Jacob. By the end of this book, I wanted more not only of them but also two other couples who had gained my interest. I have the third book in the series loaded into my Nook and ready to go. I can't wait to see where Ms. Hill will take me next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15091886684804669342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136231283" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136231283" />
    <a title="C Joy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2711937-c-joy"><img alt="C Joy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596963611p2/2711937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136231283?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C Joy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C Joy" href="/user/show/2711937-c-joy">C Joy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2711937-c-joy?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2711937-c-joy?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2711937-c-joy?shelf=erotic-fiction">erotic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2711937-c-joy?shelf=vampires-and-werewolves">vampires-and-werewolves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer136231283&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136231283" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9157513762638108907">Wow, if this story could be compared to a roller coaster, then it's one with a lot of sudden stops, drops, plunges, and loops. With this story, I'm more and more intrigued not just by the series, but by the other works of Ms Hill.<br/><br/>It started where the first one left off, with Jacob hoping for a cure for the Delilah virus, then there's Gideon's appearance, the usual characters, and they're gearing for the Council Gathering. Jacob does everything for her, and because she is his Mistress, there are </span>
  <span id="freeText9157513762638108907" style="display:none">Wow, if this story could be compared to a roller coaster, then it's one with a lot of sudden stops, drops, plunges, and loops. With this story, I'm more and more intrigued not just by the series, but by the other works of Ms Hill.<br /><br />It started where the first one left off, with Jacob hoping for a cure for the Delilah virus, then there's Gideon's appearance, the usual characters, and they're gearing for the Council Gathering. Jacob does everything for her, and because she is his Mistress, there are certain scenes where she hurts him, but not necessarily enjoys it.<br /><br />There were a lot of unpredictable scenes, but some more perceptive readers might have seen it coming. Well, I haven't and I read this with an open mind, eager for adventure. (SPOILER: I didn't rate this full a full 5 stars because of the gay sex)<br /><br />I want to borrow the words of one reviewer: “Sweet yet erotic . . . will linger in your heart long after the story is over.” That's exactly how I feel with this book. The emotions just inundated, I felt anger, anxiety, sorrow (yes, there was one point I cried), relief, and excitement.<br /><br />What I like about the characters is there's always something new to them, they're extraordinary, resilient, and in love. It was touching how, after centuries, Lyssa finally found her soulmate in Jacob, that she admitted she was ready to die before meeting him, but suddenly eternity seemed too short. There were a lot of things she gave him - her trust, her heart, mind, body, and soul - and because of this love they have that survived through different lifetimes, he didn't hesitate to offer his life.<br /><br />It's not often I read about soul-deep love, and even with the frenzy of lust, the eroticism of their acts, I felt it. Because of Ms Hill's brilliant writing, I was absorbed in this world, and feel very familiar with the characters. Their love is one that surpasses the physical and paranormal. Ms Hill wrote of a love story that is timeless. Because of that, she's now one of my favorite authors.<br /><br />The ending really hooked me in reading the next, because the author left me breathless...and anxious.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9157513762638108907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1306575679" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306575679" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312922334p2/5477946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306575679?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10983970441046123159">I can't even begin to describe my feelings about this book. It is simply amazing....AMAZING!!! The quality of writing transcends any stereotype you may have in regards to erotica. Not once did I feel like I was reading anything other than beautiful literature. The Mark is edgy, dark and overwhelmingly romantic--so much so, that I was brought to tears many times during the dynamic relationship of Jacob and Lyssa. Jacob's devotion to Lyssa is extremely heartfelt portraying loyalty and adoration. L</span>
  <span id="freeText10983970441046123159" style="display:none">I can't even begin to describe my feelings about this book. It is simply amazing....AMAZING!!! The quality of writing transcends any stereotype you may have in regards to erotica. Not once did I feel like I was reading anything other than beautiful literature. The Mark is edgy, dark and overwhelmingly romantic--so much so, that I was brought to tears many times during the dynamic relationship of Jacob and Lyssa. Jacob's devotion to Lyssa is extremely heartfelt portraying loyalty and adoration. Lyssa's love for Jacob is something that is looked down upon in her society. Her displays of affection for Jacob before the gathering is nothing compared to the lengths she would go to in protecting him. Which says alot, because her affections are absolutely wonderful to see. The introduction of Gideon and Lord Mason were equally powerful. The relationships between Jacob and Gideon/ Lyssa and Lord Mason were fantastic. The respect that Lord Mason shows Lyssa by interuppting her dance with Jacob was beautiful. <br /><br /> One of my most favorite scenes (and there were alot!) was after Lyssa's annual kill--absolutely one of the most intense intimate scenes I've ever read. I was so twisted up during the gatherering(I was actually blushing! I. was. blushing. people!!!!) --my mouth was hanging open in anticipation to all the events. The fears I had for both Jacob and Lyssa had me in tears. The level of emotion never waivered for me. I was completely mesmerized from prologue to epilogue. AMAZING, AMAZING, AMAZING!!! </span>

<div id="review_152977800" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152977800" />
    <a title="Leontine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2663609-leontine"><img alt="Leontine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597427167p2/2663609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/152977800?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leontine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leontine" href="/user/show/2663609-leontine">Leontine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2663609-leontine?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2663609-leontine?shelf=crack">crack</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer152977800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8719380122101520971">This novel is the sequel to The Vampire Queens Servant and as such this review can contain mild spoilers. Just so your warned! Right from the get-go I have to say that THE MARK OF THE VAMPIRE QUEEN is a very character and romance driven story, it doesn’t mean there wasn’t a plot, there was, it just played second violin. The torch of Jacob and Lyssa’s love burns bright which translated in sexual desires and feelings running so deep, it left a permanent mark on both main protagonists. The love unf</span>
  <span id="freeText8719380122101520971" style="display:none">This novel is the sequel to The Vampire Queens Servant and as such this review can contain mild spoilers. Just so your warned! Right from the get-go I have to say that THE MARK OF THE VAMPIRE QUEEN is a very character and romance driven story, it doesn’t mean there wasn’t a plot, there was, it just played second violin. The torch of Jacob and Lyssa’s love burns bright which translated in sexual desires and feelings running so deep, it left a permanent mark on both main protagonists. The love unfolds itself on a backdrop where a vampire society is internally vying for control and this presents danger for Lady Elyssa Amaterasu Yamato Wentworth, the last vampire queen of the Far East Clan. <br /><br />Joey W Hill immediately sets an emotionally fraught tone with a past life memory between Lyssa and Jacob, in which he was a knight, and it irrevocable drew me in. From there I felt flairs of pending danger but it was the deepening, the exploring of Jacob and Lyssa’s love that took the main stage. I slowly savored the growing bond and I got intimately acquainted with all they felt, wanted and needed. These two fascinating characters dueled with each other on every level; emotionally and physically, as with the heart and the soul. They challenged each other which translated in dynamic dialogues and along with an erotic force sizzling between them they were without a doubt each other’s match.<br /><br />Since this is the sequel I got to know Jacob and Lyssa on an even more intimate level. The devotion of Jacob to Lyssa is moving – it doesn’t make him a lesser or weaker man – oh no, far from it! He is a man ingrained with valor, strength, chivalry and honor, but it is all encompassed by a matching arrogance and Alpha attitude. He is a hero that can drive you nuts but has you loving every minute of it, just because he cares so deeply for those in his heart. <br /><br />Now Lyssa remains a captivating leading lady, she has a feral side to her, she is after all the last Vampire Queen and knows how her world works. Still, as the story progresses I got to witness more and more of her depth in the heart and soul. The intensity and extend in the way she cares, how she deems to shows that is something that I never would’ve expected reading in TVQS. She became one of those strong heroines that impresses profoundly, not by her physical strength or her Amazon attitude, but by the strength of her heart and her compassion. <br /><br />Next to the courting, the issues that arise between Jacob and Lyssa and present danger, there is also a scorching passion blazing between them. It could go form gentle loving to a male/female power clash and it was all spiced up with a bit of variation to explore the sexual appetite. I loved it, it never bored me to feel the hunger emanating between Jacob and Lyssa, and that is not where it ended. As the plot gained more attention the council gathering became a plateau of inhibitive eroticism that was very arousing. It varied from a bit of M/M to group sexing and the use of certain toys wasn’t shied from either.<br /><br />Of course there are mind games to be played, these vampires crave power and leave no chance unused to gain it. The vampire culture fascinated me with their rules, customs and rituals. I think Joey W Hill has created a great foundation for her world building and I’m eager to explore this culture further! The first half was very romance and character driven and the second half deepened on this and added a few plot twists that were hinted at in TVQS and the first half of this story. I will not go in to detail, that is for each to find out but for me the second half of the story was a perfect balance of character, romance and plot development. <br /><br />I feel like I can go on and on about the awesomeness of this series, perhaps it’s just me, that this author knows how to find my hot buttons and keeps pushing it over and over again. I feel like a fan girl squeeing about characters who will never be forgotten and how their stories keep affecting me so. The only thing I want to add is that the secondary cast of characters equally piqued my interest. I met Jacob’s brother Gideon and their shared erotic moment with Lyssa was uber sensual. Gideon is a male who demands, period. I can’t wait to find out more about this tormented vampire hunter. Next to him vampire Mason also triggered my interest and Lady Daniella from Australia with her servant Devlin are also characters I hope to meet again later in the series. <br /><br />THE MARK OF THE VAMPIRE QUEEN is an erotic romance of sheer excellence and I can understand the need for another story of Lyssa and Jacob. Their story is concluded but who doesn’t want more from such stellar characters? I feel like I’ve just been floored by a grand romance and have a hard time touching back to reality. A poignant story, that through the prose of Joey W Hill, delivered an epic romance between a vampire queen and a human servant which will deliver a thrill-ride of a read!<br /><br />4,5 stars<br /><br /><br />Quote Jacob to Gideon:<br />“So love is all about meeting your terms, is it?” Idiot, stubborn, hardheaded jackass. You used to sing me when I had a nightmare. You used to smile. Gideon turned farther away, hunching a shoulder, but to Jacob’s surprise, he responded, his voice low and gruff. “I’m past loving anyone, Jacob. I just can’t handle it anymore. This is probably just the way it’s meant to be.” The desolation in Gideon’s tone was as cold as death, and Jacob wondered if the analogy was uneasily close to the reality of his brother’s life.<br /><br />Quote Lyssa:<br />She’d left him a note, on the opposite side of the bed. “I made sure your brother took some breakfast with him. He thanked me for my hospitality and said if I ever hurt you he’d stake me out in the sunlight and happily watch me burn. I kissed him goodbye until his toes curled and he couldn’t walk without embarrassing himself. Maybe we should invite him to join us for Christmas.”<br /><br />Quote Jacob [I feel this quote really give a good definition of who Lyssa is]:<br />He looked at her and saw the vampire queen, a warrioress. A cruel tyrant, a gentle nurse. A girl. A cold, haughty bitch, a generous and loving woman. A woman who loved fiercely. She’d stayed by a husband who’d been lost to violent madness. She shielded Thomas with her own life and risked all the power she was now trying to protect, all for the benefit of other.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8719380122101520971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_109445055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109445055" />
    <a title="LMM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1533889-lmm"><img alt="LMM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393087075p2/1533889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109445055?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LMM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LMM" href="/user/show/1533889-lmm">LMM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1533889-lmm?shelf=paranormal-pnr">paranormal-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1533889-lmm?shelf=romance-or-erotica">romance-or-erotica</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109445055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9444306546013842905">I'm teetering on this actually being 3.5 to 4 stars for me. It was so, SO much better than the 1st book & I am glad Hill continued Jacob & Lyssa's story b'c it really needed more fleshing out (which it definitely got). <br/><br/>There where some eye rolling moments in the beginning (uh hem...Gideon? Really?) but I soon forgot them once I started to get to know Lyssa & Jacob a lot more. <br/><br/>Hill gave us a lot more insight into Lyssa & why she was the way she was, I started to feel more empathy for her which he</span>
  <span id="freeText9444306546013842905" style="display:none">I'm teetering on this actually being 3.5 to 4 stars for me. It was so, SO much better than the 1st book &amp; I am glad Hill continued Jacob &amp; Lyssa's story b'c it really needed more fleshing out (which it definitely got). <br /><br />There where some eye rolling moments in the beginning (uh hem...Gideon? Really?) but I soon forgot them once I started to get to know Lyssa &amp; Jacob a lot more. <br /><br />Hill gave us a lot more insight into Lyssa &amp; why she was the way she was, I started to feel more empathy for her which helped me to come around.<br /><br />Jacob is a very charming, cool MC. I like that Hill very much made him Alpha w/out the machismo - although he was really, if I am being honest, a "Gary Stu", in how he ticked so many wish fulfillment boxes. Still, I wasn't hating on him. <br /><br />IMO, It's definitely mostly a romance novel w/erotica lite mixed in &amp; really not BDSM heavy. In fact - I'm not really understanding why the 1st 2 books got labeled so heavy in that category. It's really tame by comparison to other stuff I have read. <br /><br />There was one scene where it was a bit bondage/dominance but I didn't find it heavy b'c their was a larger psychological aspect at play (vampire politics - you actually did see how the human servants are used as political pawns) that I found myself more interested in. <br /><br />There are many sex scenes, but the actions themselves are fairly redundant &amp; Hill focuses in more on describing the emotion behind the MC's in the scene rather then focusing solely on full detailed action, or body parts, etc. <br /><br />In fact many times - she'll leave the present scene &amp; have either Jacob or Lyssa's narrative segue into a memory or analysis of the meaning behind what is going on, in order to give more substance &amp; understanding to the emotional mechanism's, so when Hill snaps back to that present narrative - we have much more authentic reasoning behind it all. <br /><br />I thought she handled that really deftly. So it comes across as less smutastic &amp; more romantic with a bit of erotica lite. In fact, Hill definitely goes for playing with the heartstrings most of all.<br /><br />I found that really helped to understand the characters better so I started getting more attached &amp; liking them better &amp; better.<br /><br />I am looking forward to reading the next one (I liked these 2 characters in the last book) b'c as I said after the 1st book, I was majorly disappointed but Hill was so much better in this book, I'm hoping the buzz I heard about her is true. That she just keeps getting better &amp; better. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9444306546013842905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_68333733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68333733" />
    <a title="Sharon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/718140-sharon"><img alt="Sharon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578970921p2/718140.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68333733?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon" href="/user/show/718140-sharon">Sharon</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer68333733" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16323096130791229693">Maybe a 3.5. I really wanted to like this book more. I agree with the ratings and other reviewers - much better than the first book. But compared to other vampire books/series, this series just doesn't do it for me. I finally figured out why: I do not care for the vampire world she has created. The major difference between this world and others are the intentional cruelty and uncaring of the vampires. This completely alters the relationship between vampires and human servants, and not in an enjo</span>
  <span id="freeText16323096130791229693" style="display:none">Maybe a 3.5. I really wanted to like this book more. I agree with the ratings and other reviewers - much better than the first book. But compared to other vampire books/series, this series just doesn't do it for me. I finally figured out why: I do not care for the vampire world she has created. The major difference between this world and others are the intentional cruelty and uncaring of the vampires. This completely alters the relationship between vampires and human servants, and not in an enjoyable way for me. This was evident by the fact that I sort of plodded through this book and it took me over a week to read (which is really long for me!)<br /><br />This book is better than the first because there is less cruelty between Lyssa and Jacob. However, it still exists and the 'love' between vampires and human servants is not the kind I enjoy reading about as compared to Hamilton, Ward, etc. It's not the sex...the sex scenes are a bit 'extreme' for BDSM and whatnot, and there is some male/male action (which I'm a fan of) so the sex is fine - hot in many scenes! It's the emotional/love parts because the underlying cruelty of vampires in the 'world' Hill has created doesn't do it for me. The end was really good though so I'm glad I read the whole book. The love and emotion in the last 80 pages was what the whole series should be like!<br /><br />I believe I'm done reading the series. The next book intrigues me a little because of the characters it involves (they play secondary roles in this book) but it's still set in the same environment so I'll pass.</span>

  <span id="freeText13773810934301643028" style="display:none">Wow. I stayed up until the wee hours of the morning to finish this book because there were so many twists in the last pages that I couldn't put the thing down! I read the first book in this series and wasn't all that impressed, but admitted then that I'd have to read this sequel to find out what happened to the queen and her servant. Well, I couldn't have predicted much of this story, and I was much more impressed with it than its predecessor. One of the chief things that bothered me about the first book reared its ugly head here(and you can take that literally) and I'm no fonder of it this time. It has to do with the fact that the vampire queen had a Fey father, and what her mixed parentage does to her ... well, her servant and lover Jacob can handle it (again, literally), but it gets too close to something outside my comfort zone (which has certainly expanded of late). I realize this is all very vague, but I don't want to ruin any of the surprises this book holds in store for those who read the first book. I don't really recommend this as a stand-alone, and if you can't handle some very explicit and "out there" sex scenes, you'd best steer clear.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16643207678292626818">This is the conclusion of "The Vampire Queen's Servant", the story of ancient, beautiful Lady Lyssa and her devoted human servant Jacob. It begins where the first book left off, after Lyssa gave Jacob the third mark binding his life to hers. So much happens during the course of this book it would be nearly impossible for me to explain it all. At one point it seemed there was no way it could possibly end happily.   <span id="freeText16643207678292626818" style="display:none">This is the conclusion of "The Vampire Queen's Servant", the story of ancient, beautiful Lady Lyssa and her devoted human servant Jacob. It begins where the first book left off, after Lyssa gave Jacob the third mark binding his life to hers. So much happens during the course of this book it would be nearly impossible for me to explain it all. At one point it seemed there was no way it could possibly end happily. Somehow, magically, it does, and in a way I never would have expected.<br /><br />Joey Hill is a master of everything that you look for in a Paranormal Erotic Romance. She writes emotional, arousing erotic scenes that no other writer can even hope to touch, her world-building is beyond imaginative yet believable, and her prose is a thing of beauty. She is now without a doubt my favorite writer. Even if your not a fan of PNR, I would highly recommend reading this series. </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13884567570895629331">I love Jacob. I've always enjoyed vampire stories and found them to be sexy. Ms. Hill's vampire stories are more than sexy, erotic and hot is how they are for me. Jacob is so mixed in his feelings and his struggle to reconcile his new life is great to watch. After reading this book, I just yearn for more.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5795348-sue-davincikittie-brown-moore?shelf=joey-w-hill">joey-w-hill</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185252493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10160848073065514402">GraveTells original review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://gravetells.wordpress.com/2011/07/26/dual-review-the-vampire-queens-servant-and-the-mark-of-the-vampire-queen-the-vampire-queen-series-1-and-2-by-joey-w-hill'>http://gravetells.wordpress.com/2011/...</a><br/><br/><strong>TLDR recap:</strong><br/><br/>The oldest living vampire and the last queen of the Far East Clan, Lady Elyssa Amaterasu Yamato Wentworth, still suffers from the pain of losing her human servant and her husband.  Jacob Green is, among other things, a vampire hunter trained to hunt and kill her kind but is strangely drawn to Lyssa in ways he does not yet understand.  Even a perfect match takes a little breaking in, and Lady Lyssa excels at control.  </span>
  <span id="freeText10160848073065514402" style="display:none">GraveTells original review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://gravetells.wordpress.com/2011/07/26/dual-review-the-vampire-queens-servant-and-the-mark-of-the-vampire-queen-the-vampire-queen-series-1-and-2-by-joey-w-hill">http://gravetells.wordpress.com/2011/...</a><br /><br /><strong>TLDR recap:</strong><br /><br />The oldest living vampire and the last queen of the Far East Clan, Lady Elyssa Amaterasu Yamato Wentworth, still suffers from the pain of losing her human servant and her husband.  Jacob Green is, among other things, a vampire hunter trained to hunt and kill her kind but is strangely drawn to Lyssa in ways he does not yet understand.  Even a perfect match takes a little breaking in, and Lady Lyssa excels at control.  Struggling for dominance and honesty, Jacob and Lyssa's unusual relationship takes them far beyond the bounds accepted by both their societies and challenges the very core of their souls.<br /><br /><strong>Title:</strong> The Vampire Queen's Servant, The Mark of the Vampire Queen<br /><strong>Series:</strong> The Vampire Queen series - books #1 &amp; #2<br /><strong><strong>Author:</strong> </strong>Joey W. Hill<br /><strong>Prominent Characters:</strong> Lady Elyssa Amaterasu Yamato Wentworth, Jacob Green<br /><strong>Recommended reader age:</strong> 18+<br /><strong>Sexual content level: </strong>heavy and explicit <em>(vulgar language typical of erotica)</em><br /><br /><strong>Thoughts:</strong><br /><br />Jacob's journey toward full human servant is both tender and traumatic.  During the first novel, it is difficult to comprehend why Lyssa treats him as she does, but when all is finally revealed, it makes your heart break just a little for the both of them.  Of course, that's when you're not taking cold showers or jumping your significant other from the sheer HEAT of their chemistry.  If those book covers at the top of this post make you raise your eyebrows, well hang on to your granny panties sister cuz you ain't seen nothin' yet!  The <em>Mark of the Vampire Queen</em> has one of the hands-down-hottest scenes in a book I have ever read, eclipsing even <em>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/2011/03/06/review-one-foot-in-the-grave-night-huntress-series-2-by-jeaniene-frost/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">One Foot in the Grave</a>
</em>'s infamous Chapter 32.  The scenes in <em>The Vampire Queen's Servant</em> are no slouch either.  Ms. Hill delivers such beautiful imagery, heart-touching tenderness and discovery, amidst the visceral, intense sexual spectacles.<br /><br />These books read like one novel.  The first feels almost incomplete at the ending, knowing there is more in store for them and the battle is far from over.  To give the most honest review possible, I'm reviewing them together.  Hope you don't mind.  :)<br /><br />Now, it did take me a little while to get into the first book, but I'm so glad I stuck with it because it was <em>well</em> worth the effort.  Lyssa's attitude really annoyed me at first, and Jacob came across as a little one-dimensional.  Why would this random guy just turn his life over to this seemingly-cruel vampire he's never met?  Not knowing all the details up front makes the journey that much better as the full story unfolds.  So if you find yourself stuck, keep reading.  Get to book #2.  I promise it is worth it.<br /><br />For readers with a history of abuse, parts of this story, especially the first book, will be difficult to read.  As I continued reading, I went from apathetic about the characters to being deeply moved by them.  I think the journey will be different for each reader, based on each person's individual life experiences.  Personally, I found it complicated and not without conflict, but intensely touching.<br /><br />These stories are the perfect blend of erotica and paranormal romance, tying together a soul-deep love story and a physical connection with more sparks than a ribbon of Black Cats on the 4th.  These books pack some serious punch, so this is not for the sheltered or for readers easily offended by creative public sexual displays designed around group &amp; bondage situations!  Sound interesting yet?  It's positively <em>scandalous</em> and I DARE you to read this series!!<br /><br /><strong>Memorable quotes:</strong><br /><br />I'm quoting for two books, so get comfy!  =D<br /><br /><em>Jacob, on tattoos...</em><br /><blockquote>"It's rare to see a completely unmarked man your age.  Why is that?"<br /><br />He pulled his attention away from the thing she was treating as jewelry and he was viewing as  potential torture device.  From the slight smile on her lips, he suspected she recognized his struggle to focus.<br /><br />"My brother always said if you mark your body with a symbol, it means you stand by it forever.  Only things branded on the soul can be branded on the body.  So far I've found the only constant is that everything changes."</blockquote><br /><em>All work and no play...</em><br /><blockquote>"Yes, wicked stepmother.  I'll have everything planned to the last detail while the mice sew my dress together."  He tapped the top of the legal pad with the menu.  "You'll have the full proposal with all the details by tomorrow when you rise."</blockquote><br /><em>A servant's musing of his Mistress...</em><br /><blockquote>"She has the mindless courage of a predator, the broken heart of an angel, and a woman's unconquerable soul."</blockquote><br /><em>Life is...</em><br /><blockquote>"Life is never as dramatic as we pretend it is in a normal life.  But we can be intensely amazing, or quietly desperate, as Thoreau said.  If you woke each day with a genuine awareness which allowed you to appreciate everything as if you were seeing it for the very first time... or the last."</blockquote><br /><em>Sex: sin or devotion?</em><br /><blockquote>In fact, there was a spiritual power to it so overwhelming, Lyssa thought the religions that used it as a form of worship made more sense than those that called it a sin.</blockquote><br /><em>A jack of all trades...</em><br /><blockquote>Such was a human servant's life.  Dry cleaning, home repair, gardening.  Arranging a table centerpiece and then replacing that centerpiece to perform as a sex slave in front of dinner guests.  All in a day's work.</blockquote><br /><em>More money than God...</em><br /><blockquote>"That's such a ridiculous saying.   What use would God have for money?  Hence, a pauper has  more money than God."</blockquote><br /><br /><strong>If you like <em>The Vampire Queen's Servavnt </em>and<em> The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em> of Vampire Queen series...</strong><br /><br />If you enjoyed <em>The Vampire Queen's Servant</em>, <em>The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em>, and the rest of the Vampire Queen series for its paranormal ties (vampire society with humans who serve as blood hosts), check out the Night Huntress series (Cat &amp; Bones, starting with <em>
  <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0061245089?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=davinc-20&amp;linkCode=xm2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creativeASIN=0061245089" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Halfway to the Grave</a>
</em>) by Jeaniene Frost.  The NH books are not erotica but they feature strong ties between a central couple and they definitely have their share of steamy scenes.<br /><br /><strong>Final thoughts:</strong><br /><br />This series, <em>The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em> in particular, is seriously carnally addicting.  If I bookmarked every memorable, steamy scene, my poor book would double in size from all the squished corner pages.  The bond between Jacob and Lyssa is something truly special... for even a "normal" romance.  This is erotica with heart.  An achingly scintillating path travelled in a world of heavy dominance and submission, where sex could all-too-easily eclipse the more vulnerable and tender moments.  Even before I read the books that follow, this series was an instant favorite of mine.<br /><br />Yes, this is erotica.  Those with serious aversions to the vulgar language typically used in that genre may be uncomfortable at first.  BUT!!  Don't let that scare you!  If you're new to erotica or even new to BDSM, this is an excellent series to get you started and I highly recommend reading it.<br /><br />Sometimes a pixie sprinkles fairy dust and glitter to tempt you onto a new path, and sometimes she flits over and just drags you away with her.  You know who you are.  Thanks for convincing me to read this fantastic series!<br /><br /><strong>Rating: </strong><em>The Vampire Queen's Servant</em><br />4.5 fangs: <strong>BITE IT! </strong><br /><strong>Rating: </strong><em>The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em><br />5 fangs: <strong>DEVOUR IT! <br /><br /><strong>Related links:</strong><br /><br /><a href="http://www.storywitch.com/Books/VQS/VQS.htm" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">http://www.storywitch.com/</a> (The Vampire Queen series website)<br /><br /><a href="http://jeanienefrost.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">http://jeanienefrost.com/</a> (The Night Huntress series website)</strong></span>

<div id="review_411580410" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411580410" />
    <a title="Ruthie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1330090-ruthie"><img alt="Ruthie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335091307p2/1330090.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411580410?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruthie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruthie" href="/user/show/1330090-ruthie">Ruthie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1330090-ruthie?shelf=modern-fantasy">modern-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1330090-ruthie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1330090-ruthie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411580410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14870988493159869963">At the risk of being called shallow, I admit to usually reading erotic romances like these more for the "erotic" part than the "romance" one. In fact, I had come to realize that it has been a while since I considered the quality of the romantic elements of a book in many romance novels, be they Paranormal Romances, Urban Fantasies with Romance, Historical Romance, Erotic/Contemporary Romance, and/or Steampunk Romance. <br/><br/>Granted, when choosing a book (in no matter what genre, even-or rather-especia</span>
  <span id="freeText14870988493159869963" style="display:none">At the risk of being called shallow, I admit to usually reading erotic romances like these more for the "erotic" part than the "romance" one. In fact, I had come to realize that it has been a while since I considered the quality of the romantic elements of a book in many romance novels, be they Paranormal Romances, Urban Fantasies with Romance, Historical Romance, Erotic/Contemporary Romance, and/or Steampunk Romance. <br /><br />Granted, when choosing a book (in no matter what genre, even-or rather-especially YA) I go for those with at least one love story sub-plot. However, since Romance novels and YA had become so cliche in their sorry excuse for a good love story or even underlying sexual tension between the male and female lead; I had become desensitized to any chemistry the authors would try (but many times fail to actually do) to inject into their novels. So I had begun to read for a good plot, action, adventure, mystery, likeable characters I can relate to and yes, hot steamy sex/sexual tension. Who cares about romance? Nobody seems to make it real enough for me to get into it. (I swear! The lines the male leads usually utter are like they were paraphrased from 90's boy bands' lyrics).<br /><br /><b>But this book and its prequel however, turned out to be a very very nice surprise for me in the Romantic department.</b> Somehow, despite the dark theme of this book and the paranormal elements, the romance between the lead characters felt real. Their dilemma was REAL (yeah Edward and Bella - they had real issues why it was hard for them to be together).<br /><br />I loved Jacob! He was a different type of alpha male. Most alpha males in the PNR genre seem interchangeable to me (except for Barrons in Karen Moning's Fever series). I loved how he tried to stand by the morals he believed in and his dilemma when it came to choosing the woman he loved over them. How he almost walked away from his vampire queen but how he decided to stay - that's what's real! Not the "i will burn the world for you" - typical hero type.<br /><br />I liked Lyssa too. She was unlike any other heroine in the romances I've read. Well, of course, she's over a millennia old - so yeah, she would act more mature than most female characters in other books, but you could relate to her when her heart warred with her head. Her obligations warring with her desires. <br /><br />Good chemistry and good character development! Kudos Ms. Hill!<br /><br />The sex was hot and steamy. The BSDM scenes were not as many or even as wild as Anne Rice's Sleeping Beauty trilogy, but unlike the Sleeping Beauty books - where all sexual acts just seemed like a big role playing game, the BDSM here was life threatening in a way because of the world the characters were placed in - where humans were very much disposable to vampires. Hence, it upped the ante of some (not all) of the sex scenes.<br /><br />I will miss Jacob and Lyssa, since apparently the next books in the series won't be about them :( But in any case, these were enjoyable reads :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14870988493159869963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_151733258" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151733258" />
    <a title="Jennifer " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3198681-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372568236p2/3198681.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151733258?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer " href="/user/show/3198681-jennifer">Jennifer </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=bd-sm">bd-sm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=vamps">vamps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=erotic-romance">erotic-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=male-male">male-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3198681-jennifer?shelf=so-good-i-re-read-it">so-good-i-re-read-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151733258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3287870978822018697">I feel so amazed and thankful to find another series and author that I LOVE. I've had a lot of luck in that regard in the last year or so. After Twilight and BDB, there were series I liked a lot, but nothing amazing, that captured me wholly and completely. Then came Outlander (the best!) and the Fever series. But finally, I've found another vamp series that transcends!!!!! <br/>I don't know if I can put into words what I feel after reading this book. If you've read my first review, you know how much </span>
  <span id="freeText3287870978822018697" style="display:none">I feel so amazed and thankful to find another series and author that I LOVE. I've had a lot of luck in that regard in the last year or so. After Twilight and BDB, there were series I liked a lot, but nothing amazing, that captured me wholly and completely. Then came Outlander (the best!) and the Fever series. But finally, I've found another vamp series that transcends!!!!! <br />I don't know if I can put into words what I feel after reading this book. If you've read my first review, you know how much I loved the first in the series, the intro to Jacob and Lyssa's story. This is the conclusion. I wish I could pinpoint what is so different about these books compared to standard popular paranormal romance. Certainly it's more erotic and there's a very D/s feel to certain parts. But that's not the soul of this book. I think it's the depth of characterization as well as the lush narrative that set it apart. That and the seriousness of it all. I actually have a big pet peeve when it comes to paranormal authors trivializing death and violence. This may be fantasy, but when characters maim/attempt to kill each other without any emotional weight, it invalidates many of the emotions they seem to develop later in the story for me. These books are very serious in that regard. That's not to say that they are not violent. Most characters here are morally ambiguous and very complex. But we feel the finality of death, the torment of those left behind as perpetrators of that destruction. There is humor here too in the natural dialog, especially in the scenes with Jacob's brother, Gideon, the vampire hunter who has to come to terms with his brother's calling to be a vampire servant. There are some outrageous behaviors which were entertaining. At the annual Gathering of all vampire lords and ladies and their servants, the behavior is reminiscent of Anne Rice's Sleeping Beauty series. <br />The depth of love, of one's capacity to serve so perfectly and selflessly is captured beautifully. I shed so many tears! Jacob is the ultimate alpha who serves his woman and works to have her call HIM Master, even in a world where that isn't permitted. The romance is VERY sweep you off your feet and so intense it was hard to look away. I basically read this in one night, which is crazy! Oh, and to top it all, Joey Hill has her vamps doing thinks like quoting Thoreau! (in a non-pretentious, so perfect way). She is a VERY smart writer. I'll never understand why such talent can't be recognized on a greater scale. It's the fate of erotica, I guess, but I want to shout out to the world that this is such awesome writing, she needs to be recognized! <br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3287870978822018697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1810122527" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5723625-angel-huge-fan-of-all-things-totoro?shelf=made-me-smile">made-me-smile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5723625-angel-huge-fan-of-all-things-totoro?shelf=awesome">awesome</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1810122527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14595254784850390797">“The Mark of the Vampire Queen” was much more interesting than the first book. Don’t get me wrong, I loved seeing Jacob get under Lady Lyssa’s defenses, making her care more for him than she should for a servant. By the second book, we have a feel of their unique relationship. Jacob knows when and when not to push Lady Lyssa, especially since she could kill him with a flick of her finger.<br/><br/>This book starts off reminding us that Lady Lyssa only has so much time to live. We get introduced to Gideon,</span>
  <span id="freeText14595254784850390797" style="display:none">“The Mark of the Vampire Queen” was much more interesting than the first book. Don’t get me wrong, I loved seeing Jacob get under Lady Lyssa’s defenses, making her care more for him than she should for a servant. By the second book, we have a feel of their unique relationship. Jacob knows when and when not to push Lady Lyssa, especially since she could kill him with a flick of her finger.<br /><br />This book starts off reminding us that Lady Lyssa only has so much time to live. We get introduced to Gideon, Jacob’s vampire hunter brother. Even though Gideon was only there for a short time, I felt sympathy for his chaotic emotions. He lost someone he loved to a vampire, so of course his path was chosen for him. Amazingly, I actually liked the scene where Lady Lyssa helps him relieve some of his rage and pain by giving him her body. Yes, he hates vampires, but a small part of him thanked Lady Lyssa for what she did.<br /><br />Yes, they had sex. With Jacob. The brothers basically made a Lyssa sandwich. Sooo hot.<br /><br />For such an erotic book, the characters felt so damn real to me. They breathed, they moved, they loved, and it didn’t feel at all fake. I could see them as clear as day. Hell, even characters that only had a few scenes or came in late in the book felt real. The entire world Joey Hill has created is amazing. I will definitely read the next book in the series because I don’t want to say goodbye to this world.<br /><br />The whole giant orgy thing was not what I had expected. Joey Hill isn’t afraid to show us that sex between a man and a woman isn’t the only thing out there. I won’t go into detail, but holy hot dayum. Get a fan when you get to the point where Jacob, Debra, Devlin, and Malachi get together.<br /><br />When Carnal and his evil followers reveal to the vampire hunters the location of the Council, shit hits the fan. At the same time, the virus that Lady Lyssa has reaches the final stages. She and Jacob nearly die from it, but the cure is found just in time. I felt that was a little too convenient. I saw it coming a mile away. What I did NOT see was Lady Lyssa losing her vampire/human form and becoming a true Fey, which looks kinda like a gargoyle with wicked fangs, claws, and wings. She turns Jacob at the last moment, but loses her form.<br /><br />The Vampires decide to kill her because of her “deception”, but change their minds when their lives are threatened by the hunters. In the end, Lady Lyssa leaves Jacob because she doesn’t want him to get hurt and she will be hunted; and because he needs to be trained as a new vampire, something she cannot do because she no longer is a vampire herself.<br /><br />Confusing, I know.<br /><br />In the end, they are together, pregnant. I was so damn happy to see the ending, but I still wanted their story to continue. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14595254784850390797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2798374541287915722">First off let me say that I loved The Vampire Queen's Servant. This is part two in Jacob's quest to win his masters heart and soul. I will not say that you must read the first one... but to understand the world that Ms. Hill has created for these two and what they have gone through to get there, you really should read the first one.<br/><br/>Okay... moving forward...<br/><br/>The romance between Jacob and Lady Lyssa is very breathtaking. Their relationship blossoms into the fullest it possibly can. Jacob has receiv</span>
  <span id="freeText2798374541287915722" style="display:none">First off let me say that I loved The Vampire Queen's Servant. This is part two in Jacob's quest to win his masters heart and soul. I will not say that you must read the first one... but to understand the world that Ms. Hill has created for these two and what they have gone through to get there, you really should read the first one.<br /><br />Okay... moving forward...<br /><br />The romance between Jacob and Lady Lyssa is very breathtaking. Their relationship blossoms into the fullest it possibly can. Jacob has received his third mark; which means that he has bound himself to his Master until death. Imagine saying our wedding, you say: till death do us part... now imagine if that were true, your spouse died, you died with him/her. This book does not deter away from the BDSM parts of Ms Hill's style. Her writing style just simply amazes me. To read her books (the two that I have) will throw you in a world of her very own. Be prepared to go on a journey you will sure to be enthralled in.<br /><br />Lady Lyssa is slowly dying and Jacob will do everything in his power to stop that from happening. Along with her sickness, there is the meeting coming before the Council. Lady Lyssa is trying to pave a better future for the vampires. One of her goals is to address the issue of permanent asylum for the fugitives in her territory. And the other is to push for them to become more civilized by only needing to kill one human a year for them to maintain their strength. But some vampires do not agree with her thinking and want to over throw the Council. and her. So the plot thickens...<br /><br />I will tell you this though, this story left me wanting more... It's in the ending, but I am not quiet sure where and that is my problem. I am not sure if her being of two heritages got me, or that she shifted, or that the love did not go the way I wanted it too (yea, I am selfish like that) or what... but something was missing for me. Maybe the power struggle... the grand ending. I will struggle with this and it will bother me... Because I love this woman's writing!!<br /><br />I love what has become of Jacob and his Master. The journey he goes to get there. If there is a man out there like Jacob... oh please let yourself be known! This man will do anything, everything and back again for his woman. OMG... Jacob remains my Sex on a Stick man.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2798374541287915722" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176486296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11737950627095439130">The Mark of the Vampire Queen was a very hard one for me to finish, purely because it bored me.<br/><br/>Jacob is now a full servant of the vampire queen Lyssa. With this title comes the knowledge that Lyssa is very sick and dying, and now, because of his new stature, so will he die along with her.<br/><br/>This pains the pair of them as in their own way, they love each other, being soul mates throughout Lyssa’s incomparably long life and Jacob through his various incarnations, to have found each other in this capa</span>
  <span id="freeText11737950627095439130" style="display:none">The Mark of the Vampire Queen was a very hard one for me to finish, purely because it bored me.<br /><br />Jacob is now a full servant of the vampire queen Lyssa. With this title comes the knowledge that Lyssa is very sick and dying, and now, because of his new stature, so will he die along with her.<br /><br />This pains the pair of them as in their own way, they love each other, being soul mates throughout Lyssa’s incomparably long life and Jacob through his various incarnations, to have found each other in this capacity Jacob wants to hold on to as her for as long as he can.<br /><br />I will be quite frank and say that this book bored me literally to sleep. There was far too much detail wrapped up in politics and medieval fairs that I had to force myself to finish just to have the pleasure of writing this review. The politics interest me, but the way they were written in reminding me of watching Parliament Time on the ABC, a lot of people talking quietly for two hours and once every three months having a raving blue with each other that can be quite entertaining.<br /><br />I originally picked up this series because I read an excerpt of book five, Vampire Mistress, and thought it intriguing. It might still be, it’s just a shame that I will not get to it because of the quality of the first two books.<br /><br />In hindsight I remember the first book being relatively slow, to the point of having to force myself through it as well. There just isn’t enough driving this story for me to enjoy it. Sure you have a problem in the form of Lyssa’s impending doom and the effect it will have on Jacob, you also have the likes of Carnal trying to upset the order Lyssa has been trying to build between vampires and humans for the last thousand years.<br /><br />Yet when it’s put on paper in the way that Hill writes it, it just drags on and on. In the end I was marking chapter ends so I felt a small victory each time I reached one.<br /><br />The sex was hot in this series overall, I will admit that, some of the scenes Hill came up with were especially well written, but there just wasn’t enough built around those scenes for me to remotely enjoy this story at all.<br /><br />Find this review at storywings.com</span>

<div id="review_91542693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/91542693" />
    <a title="Jill Dunlop" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3348876-jill-dunlop"><img alt="Jill Dunlop" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267370140p2/3348876.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91542693?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill Dunlop" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill Dunlop" href="/user/show/3348876-jill-dunlop">Jill Dunlop</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91542693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer267262418992540695"><em>The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em> picks up right where <em>The Vampire Queen's Servant</em> left off. Lyssa is sick with an unknown disease that currently has no cure. Jacob her human servant is bound to her, which means when she dies he will too. Lyssa controls the Vampire territory of the Southeastern United States and is one of the most influencial members of the Vampire Council. Before she succombs to this illness, she needs to make sure her Vampires will have sanctuary when she dies. At the next council</span>
  <span id="freeText267262418992540695" style="display:none"><em>The Mark of the Vampire Queen</em> picks up right where <em>The Vampire Queen's Servant</em> left off. Lyssa is sick with an unknown disease that currently has no cure. Jacob her human servant is bound to her, which means when she dies he will too. Lyssa controls the Vampire territory of the Southeastern United States and is one of the most influencial members of the Vampire Council. Before she succombs to this illness, she needs to make sure her Vampires will have sanctuary when she dies. At the next council meeting she plans to bring this issue forth to the council. There are several obsticals that make this next to impossible to accomplish, Carnal a sadistic vampire out to demolish the Council, Jacob's vampire-hunter brother Gabriel, and Lyssa's illness.<br /><br />This book really pushes the envelope, so to speak. Some of the things in this book made me uncomfortable. I think that was the author's intent, though. One of the aspects to Lyssa and Jacob's relationship is that they would both push the boundaries on what they were comfortable with. Lyssa would push Jacob to do things sexually that he normally would never think to do, nor imagine that they would arouse him as they do. In turn, Jacob would make Lyssa realize how much more her heart and soul was involved when having sex with Jacob. She was much more deeply involved with him than she has ever been with anyone else. So this was a very interesting dynamic to read.<br /><br />I felt the pacing of the first half of the book was a little slow. Halfway through when Jacob and Lyssa attend the council meeting things really begin to pick up. When it came time for the climax of the story, I was hanging onto the edge of my seat. It was very intense, as there was a lot to take in and alot the characters had to deal with. I was surprised at the range of emotions I went through and came to realize that I had really connected to Jacob and Lyssa. I definitely want to continue with more of this series. I think Joey W. Hill is one of the better erotic romance authors I have read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="267262418992540695" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Gladys (glad4twilight)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gladys (glad4twilight)" href="/user/show/4746026-gladys-glad4twilight">Gladys (glad4twilight)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4746026-gladys-glad4twilight?shelf=bdsm">bdsm</a>,
